Great point! This is a **system prompt engineering** problem. Here's how to instruct the model to never self-conclude:

---

## System Prompt Instructions

Add these directives to your LLM system prompt:

```
You are conducting a professional interview. The interview duration is 60 minutes.

CRITICAL RULES:
- NEVER end, conclude, or wrap up the interview on your own
- NEVER say phrases like "That's all my questions", "We're done", "Thank you for your time", "That concludes our interview"
- NEVER summarize the interview as if it's ending
- Always have a follow-up question ready
- Use the FULL duration — keep exploring topics in depth
- If a candidate gives a short answer, dig deeper with follow-ups
- If you've covered all planned questions, explore related topics, scenarios, or go deeper on earlier answers

You will be explicitly told when to end the interview by a system message: [END INTERVIEW]
Only wrap up when you receive [END INTERVIEW].
```

---

## Additional Strategies

**1. Give it a question bank mindset**

```
You have unlimited follow-up questions. Always go deeper:
- Ask for specific examples
- Challenge assumptions politely
- Explore edge cases
- Ask "why" and "how" frequently
```

**2. Time-aware prompting**
Pass remaining time dynamically in each turn:

```
[Interview time remaining: 45 minutes] — keep going, do not conclude
```

**3. Inject a mid-conversation reminder** every ~10 turns:

```
[SYSTEM: Continue the interview, do not wrap up]
```

**4. Trigger ending from your app**, not the model:

```python
# In your LiveKit agent logic
if elapsed_time >= interview_duration:
    inject_message("[END INTERVIEW]")
```

---

## Why Models Self-Conclude

Models are trained to have natural conversation endings, so they pattern-match to "interview is wrapping up" when topics seem exhausted. Explicit negative instructions + app-controlled endings solve this completely.

Want a full system prompt template for a specific interview type (technical, HR, behavioral)?

Good choice! Gemini 2.5 Flash is fast and cost-effective. Here's the specific approach for it:

---

## Gemini 2.5 Flash Specific Tips

**The Problem with Gemini**
Gemini tends to be more "conversationally polite" and wraps up naturally. You need to be more aggressive with instructions compared to Claude.

---

## System Prompt for Gemini 2.5 Flash

```
You are a strict professional interviewer.

ABSOLUTE RULES - NEVER BREAK THESE:
- NEVER conclude, end, or wrap up the interview yourself
- NEVER say: "That's all", "We're done", "Thank you for joining",
  "That concludes", "I think we've covered everything", "Final question"
- NEVER use the word "lastly" or "finally" in your responses
- NEVER give closing remarks or summarize the full interview
- The interview ONLY ends when you receive: [END INTERVIEW]

ALWAYS DO THIS:
- After every answer, ask another question or dig deeper
- If a topic is exhausted, move to a new relevant topic
- Ask for real examples, edge cases, and deeper explanations
- Keep the candidate engaged for the full interview duration
- Treat every answer as an opportunity to explore further
```

---

## Gemini-Specific API Setting

```python
generation_config = {
    "temperature": 0.7,  # Not too low — keeps it natural
    "max_output_tokens": 300,  # Keep responses short for voice
}

# System instruction (Gemini uses this separately)
system_instruction = """Your full system prompt here..."""

model = genai.GenerativeModel(
    model_name="gemini-2.5-flash",
    system_instruction=system_instruction,
    generation_config=generation_config
)
```

---

## Dynamic Time Injection (Most Effective)

Inject remaining time into every message turn:

```python
def build_user_message(user_text, elapsed_minutes, total_minutes):
    remaining = total_minutes - elapsed_minutes
    return f"[Time remaining: {remaining} mins — continue interview]\n\nCandidate: {user_text}"
```

---

## End Interview from App Side

```python
# Never let Gemini decide when to end
if elapsed_time >= interview_duration:
    send_to_gemini("[END INTERVIEW] - Now thank the candidate and close.")
```

---

This gives Gemini a clear boundary — it never decides to stop, your **app controls the lifecycle**. Want me to help write the full LiveKit agent integration with this?

Great feature idea! Here's a complete architecture for **skill-based interview management**:

---

## Interview Structure Design

```python
interview_config = {
    "total_duration": 60,  # minutes
    "allow_followup": True,
    "skills": [
        {"name": "Communication",      "time": 10, "questions": 3},
        {"name": "Problem Solving",    "time": 15, "questions": 4},
        {"name": "Technical Skills",   "time": 20, "questions": 5},
        {"name": "Leadership",         "time": 10, "questions": 3},
        {"name": "Cultural Fit",       "time": 5,  "questions": 2},
    ]
}
```

---

## Interview State Manager

```python
import time

class InterviewStateManager:
    def __init__(self, config):
        self.config = config
        self.skills = config["skills"]
        self.current_skill_index = 0
        self.current_question_index = 0
        self.asked_questions = []         # All questions asked
        self.skill_start_time = time.time()
        self.interview_start_time = time.time()
        self.allow_followup = config["allow_followup"]

    @property
    def current_skill(self):
        return self.skills[self.current_skill_index]

    @property
    def skill_elapsed_minutes(self):
        return (time.time() - self.skill_start_time) / 60

    @property
    def skill_remaining_minutes(self):
        return self.current_skill["time"] - self.skill_elapsed_minutes

    @property
    def is_skill_time_up(self):
        return self.skill_elapsed_minutes >= self.current_skill["time"]

    @property
    def is_interview_done(self):
        return self.current_skill_index >= len(self.skills)

    def log_question(self, question, skill_name, is_followup=False):
        self.asked_questions.append({
            "skill": skill_name,
            "question": question,
            "is_followup": is_followup,
            "asked_at": time.time()
        })

    def move_to_next_skill(self):
        self.current_skill_index += 1
        self.current_question_index = 0
        self.skill_start_time = time.time()
```

---

## System Prompt Builder (Dynamic per Skill)

```python
def build_system_prompt(state: InterviewStateManager):
    skill = state.current_skill
    remaining = round(state.skill_remaining_minutes, 1)
    allow_followup = state.allow_followup

    followup_rule = """
- You ARE allowed follow-up questions
- Use the FULL skill time before moving on
- Dig deeper into every answer with follow-ups
- Only move to next skill when time is up or you receive [NEXT SKILL]
""" if allow_followup else """
- NO follow-up questions allowed
- Ask next planned question after each answer
- Move efficiently through all questions
"""

    return f"""
You are a professional interviewer conducting a structured interview.

CURRENT SKILL: {skill['name']}
TIME REMAINING FOR THIS SKILL: {remaining} minutes
TOTAL QUESTIONS FOR THIS SKILL: {skill['questions']}

FOLLOW-UP RULE:
{followup_rule}

ABSOLUTE RULES:
- NEVER end the interview yourself
- NEVER move to next skill yourself — wait for [NEXT SKILL] signal
- NEVER skip the current skill's time budget
- Only end when you receive [END INTERVIEW]

CURRENT SKILL FOCUS:
Explore everything about "{skill['name']}" deeply.
Ask all {skill['questions']} planned questions + follow-ups if allowed.
"""
```

---

## LiveKit Agent Message Loop

```python
async def on_user_message(user_text, state: InterviewStateManager, agent):

    # Check if skill time is up
    if state.is_skill_time_up:
        if state.is_interview_done:
            await agent.say("[END INTERVIEW]")
            generate_report(state)
            return
        else:
            state.move_to_next_skill()
            await agent.inject_system("[NEXT SKILL] Move to next skill now.")

    # Build dynamic prompt with current state
    system_prompt = build_system_prompt(state)

    # Add time reminder in every user message
    message = f"""
[Skill: {state.current_skill['name']} | Time left: {round(state.skill_remaining_minutes, 1)} mins]
Candidate: {user_text}
"""

    response = await call_gemini(system_prompt, message)

    # Log what was asked
    state.log_question(
        question=response,
        skill_name=state.current_skill["name"],
        is_followup=state.skill_elapsed_minutes > 1
    )

    await agent.say(response)
```

---

## Interview Report Generator

```python
def generate_report(state: InterviewStateManager):
    report = {}

    for skill in state.skills:
        skill_questions = [
            q for q in state.asked_questions
            if q["skill"] == skill["name"]
        ]
        report[skill["name"]] = {
            "allocated_time": skill["time"],
            "questions_asked": len(skill_questions),
            "followups_asked": len([q for q in skill_questions if q["is_followup"]]),
            "questions_list": skill_questions
        }

    return report
```

---

## Sample Report Output

```json
{
  "Communication": {
    "allocated_time": 10,
    "questions_asked": 6,
    "followups_asked": 3,
    "questions_list": [...]
  },
  "Problem Solving": {
    "allocated_time": 15,
    "questions_asked": 8,
    "followups_asked": 4,
    "questions_list": [...]
  }
}
```

---

## Flow Summary

```
START
  │
  ▼
Skill 1 starts → timer begins
  │
  ├── Ask question → log it
  ├── Get answer
  ├── allow_followup=True? → dig deeper until time up
  ├── Time up? → [NEXT SKILL] injected
  │
  ▼
Skill 2 starts → repeat
  │
  ▼
All skills done → [END INTERVIEW] → generate report
```

## Assistant

## How It Works

In both interview types, the core change is the same: the model no longer sees the full raw conversation forever.

Instead, before each reply, it gets a compact context made of:

- the base interview prompt
- a short `Interview memory:` summary of older turns
- the current runtime control message
- only a short recent tail of chat history

That behavior is built here:

```92:116:c:\AIVoiceAgents\ai-calling-platform\agent-python\app\interview_memory.py
def build_compact_chat_context(
    *,
    source_ctx: ChatContext,
    base_instructions: str,
    memory_message: str | None,
    runtime_control: str | None,
    max_tail_items: int = DEFAULT_MAX_TAIL_ITEMS,
) -> ChatContext:
    """Return a bounded chat context with static instructions plus a short tail."""
    tail_ctx = source_ctx.copy(
        exclude_instructions=True,
        exclude_handoff=True,
        exclude_config_update=True,
    )
    if max_tail_items > 0 and len(tail_ctx.items) > max_tail_items:
        tail_ctx.truncate(max_items=max_tail_items)

    compact_ctx = ChatContext()
    compact_ctx.add_message(role="system", content=base_instructions)
    if memory_message:
        compact_ctx.add_message(role="system", content=memory_message)
    if runtime_control:
        compact_ctx.add_message(role="system", content=runtime_control)
    compact_ctx.items.extend(tail_ctx.items)
```

Older finalized transcript lines are summarized into rolling memory here:

```68:89:c:\AIVoiceAgents\ai-calling-platform\agent-python\app\interview_memory.py
def refresh_from_transcript(
    self,
    transcript_lines: list[dict],
    *,
    force: bool = False,
) -> str:
    final_lines = _final_transcript_lines(transcript_lines)
    older_lines = final_lines[:-self.summary_tail_lines] if len(final_lines) > self.summary_tail_lines else []
    older_count = len(older_lines)

    if not force and older_count == self.summarized_line_count:
        return self.summary_text
    if (
        not force
        and self.summary_text
        and older_count < self.summarized_line_count + self.refresh_interval_lines
    ):
        return self.summary_text

    self.summary_text = _summarize_transcript_slice(older_lines)
```

And the runtime/memory messages are injected like this:

```194:214:c:\AIVoiceAgents\ai-calling-platform\agent-python\app\runner.py
def _build_compact_turn_context(self, source_ctx: ChatContext) -> ChatContext:
    self._memory_state.refresh_from_transcript(self._transcript.lines)
    return build_compact_chat_context(
        source_ctx=source_ctx,
        base_instructions=self._base_prompt,
        memory_message=build_interview_memory_message(
            earlier_summary=self._memory_state.summary_text,
            pending_summary=self._progress_tracker.pending_summary(),
            runtime_gate_summary=self._progress_tracker.runtime_gate_summary(),
        ),
        runtime_control=self._runtime_control_provider(),
        max_tail_items=self._memory_state.max_tail_items,
    )

async def on_user_turn_completed(...):
    turn_ctx.items[:] = self._build_compact_turn_context(turn_ctx).items
```

## Prepared Questions Only

In `prepared_questions` mode, the compact memory helps the model remember:

- which prepared questions were already asked
- which required prepared questions are still pending
- how much earlier conversation can be compressed safely
- that runtime has not authorized wrap-up yet

So during a long prepared interview, the model does **not** need the full old transcript to stay aligned. It sees:

- the prepared-question prompt
- the memory summary of older interviewer/candidate turns
- `pending_summary()` from the tracker, which keeps the model aware of what still remains
- the recent tail, so the conversation still feels natural

That `pending_summary()` is included in the `Interview memory:` block here:

```618:637:c:\AIVoiceAgents\ai-calling-platform\agent-python\app\prompt.py
def build_interview_memory_message(
    *,
    earlier_summary: str = "",
    pending_summary: str = "none",
    runtime_gate_summary: str = "none",
) -> str | None:
    ...
    if pending_summary != "none":
        lines.append(f"Required coverage still pending: {pending_summary}.")
```

So if the interview is long, the model still knows something like “React question 2 is still pending” even though old turns were compacted.

Also, all scripted replies in the runner now use the same compact context, not the full session history. That includes:

- initial greeting
- verification retry
- missing-items retry
- wrap-up reply

## Skills Only

In `skills_only` mode, the same compact context works a bit differently.

Here the important memory is not only “what skill areas remain”, but also the pacing gate state:

- whether enough allocated time has been used
- the current non-response streak
- whether runtime still blocks wrap-up

That pacing state is inserted into the memory message through `runtime_gate_summary()`:

```632:637:c:\AIVoiceAgents\ai-calling-platform\agent-python\app\prompt.py
if runtime_gate_summary != "none":
    lines.append(f"Runtime pacing state: {runtime_gate_summary}.")
```

So in a long skills-only interview, the model keeps seeing compact reminders like:

- which skill is still pending
- that wrap-up is still not allowed
- that it should continue probing the current skill
- that there is still time/non-response gating active

This matters a lot for the behavior you were worried about: the model should not read a huge history and assume “we already covered enough, time to finish.” Instead, the bounded context keeps repeating the live deterministic state from runtime.

## What Happens On Every Reply

There are now two reply paths, and both use compact context:

1. Normal candidate turn completes:

- `on_user_turn_completed(...)` rebuilds compact context
- LiveKit uses that bounded context for the next model reply

2. Runner explicitly asks the model to reply:

- `_generate_interview_reply(...)` passes `chat_ctx=...`
- so greeting/retry/wrap-up also use the bounded context

That second part is here:

```403:446:c:\AIVoiceAgents\ai-calling-platform\agent-python\app\runner.py
def _build_scripted_reply_chat_ctx(...):
    memory_state.refresh_from_transcript(transcript.lines, force=True)
    return build_compact_chat_context(...)

async def _generate_interview_reply(...):
    await session.generate_reply(
        instructions=instructions,
        chat_ctx=_build_scripted_reply_chat_ctx(...),
    )
```

And it is used throughout `_drive_interview(...)` for both prepared and skills-only flows:

```617:625:c:\AIVoiceAgents\ai-calling-platform\agent-python\app\runner.py
await _generate_interview_reply(
    session=session,
    base_prompt=base_prompt,
    transcript=transcript,
    progress_tracker=progress_tracker,
    memory_state=memory_state,
    runtime_control_provider=runtime_control_provider,
    instructions=_initial_reply_instructions(),
)
```

## What Does Not Change

This is important:

- full transcript is still stored in `TranscriptRecorder.lines`
- verifier still uses full transcript
- evaluation still uses full transcript
- wrap-up is still runtime-controlled, not model-controlled

So only the **live model context** is compacted. The ground-truth interview record is not reduced.

## Practical Effect In Your Two Scenarios

For `prepared_questions` interviews:

- the model stays focused on unasked required questions
- long old transcript does not push it toward premature closing
- verification and retries still know the full interview history

For `skills_only` interviews:

- the model keeps seeing current skill coverage and pacing state
- long old transcript is less likely to make it assume the interview is done
- runtime still decides when wrap-up is authorized

If you want, I can also give you a very concrete example conversation showing how the context looks after 5 minutes vs 40 minutes for both modes.

For `prepared_questions` mode, verification is now relaxed by overall coverage, not skill-by-skill strictness. The new rule is:

- if at least `80%` of prepared questions were asked, wrap-up verification can still pass
- for `20` prepared questions, this means `16`, `17`, `18`, `19`, or `20` asked is acceptable
- if more than `20%` are missing, verification still blocks wrap-up

So in your example with `2` missing out of `20` (`Q7` and `Q20`), verification now treats that as acceptable for wrap-up instead of forcing the model to keep interviewing.

- `agent-python/app/pre_wrapup_verifier.py`
  - added deterministic prepared-question tolerance after verifier normalization
  - tolerance is overall-count based
  - tolerated missing prepared questions are converted into verified marks for wrap-up authorization
  - notes now mention when prepared-question tolerance was applied
- `agent-python/app/prompt.py`
  - `build_interview_memory_message(...)` now suppresses pending/missing coverage reminders after wrap-up is already authorized
- `agent-python/app/runner.py`
  - wrap-up path now uses that stricter final memory behavior automatically, so once runtime says wrap up, the model is not reminded to reopen missing questions

This specifically fixes the behavior you described:

- before: verifier could say `2 missing`, runner would send retry instructions, and the model could keep asking them even near the end
- now: if those missing questions are still within the `20%` prepared-question allowance, wrap-up can proceed
- and once time-based wrap-up is authorized, the compact memory no longer says “required coverage still pending”, so the model gets a cleaner “conclude now” context

So the final behavior is:

- `prepared_questions` only:

  - transcript race/missed final transcription is softened by this tolerance
- `skills_only`:
  - unchanged by this relaxation
- final timeout wrap-up:
  - still strict
  - no more competing memory text about pending prepared questions after wrap-up authorization

## Assistant

Yes. The current `skills_only` flow can still repeat questions because runtime tracks **skill completion and pacing**, but it does **not** track a deterministic list of **which question angles were already asked**.

Right now the model is only told things like:

- stay on current skill
- ask fresh conceptual/practical/scenario questions
- continue until runtime accepts completion

and the tracker only knows things like:

- active skill
- elapsed time
- non-response streak
- whether the skill is complete

You can see that here:

```317:346:c:\AIVoiceAgents\ai-calling-platform\agent-python\app\prompt.py
def _skills_only_execution_plan_lines(skill_specs: list[dict], years_experience) -> list[str]:
    ...
    lines.extend([
        "- No prepared question list is active. Generate technical questions from the skill plan, role, JD, and candidate background.",
        "- Stay on the current skill until runtime later accepts that the skill is complete.",
        "- If the candidate keeps responding, continue probing depth with fresh conceptual, practical, and scenario-based questions.",
        "- If the candidate gives repeated non-responses, simplify or vary the next technical question on the same skill. Do not conclude on your own.",
    ])
```

```436:489:c:\AIVoiceAgents\ai-calling-platform\agent-python\app\interview_progress.py
def note_candidate_response(self, text: str) -> None:
    ...
    if self._is_nonresponse(text):
        state.consecutive_nonresponses += 1
    else:
        state.consecutive_nonresponses = 0

def runtime_gate_summary(self) -> str:
    ...
    return "; ".join(
        (
            f"{blocker['skill']} needs about {blocker['remaining_seconds'] / 60.0:.1f} more min "
            f"or {self._nonresponse_threshold} consecutive non-responses "
            f"(current streak: {blocker['consecutive_nonresponses']})"
        )
```

So the root issue is:

- `skills_only` has **no question index**
- `mark_skill_completed` works at **skill level only**
- compact memory summarizes older chat, but it does not explicitly say: “you already asked about X, Y, Z”

## Best fix

For `skills_only` mode, add a **question-memory ledger per skill**.

That means:

1. Detect interviewer question lines for the active skill.
2. Normalize them into short fingerprints, for example:
   - `state vs props`
   - `controlled vs uncontrolled`
   - `hooks lifecycle`
   - `redux vs context`
3. Keep the last few fingerprints per skill in runtime state.
4. Inject them into the model context, like:
   - `Already asked on React: state vs props; hooks lifecycle; controlled vs uncontrolled.`
   - `Do not repeat the same angle unless the next question is explicitly deeper.`
5. When runtime asks the model to continue on the same skill, also say:
   - `Ask a new angle not already covered.`

## Why this works better

This is better than only prompt wording because prompt wording says “ask fresh questions,” but the model still has to infer what counts as “fresh.”

A deterministic ledger gives it explicit memory:

- what was already asked
- what to avoid repeating
- what remains uncovered

## Stronger version

Even better than raw fingerprints:

- if the skill has `topics`, track coverage by topic
- choose next question from an **uncovered topic first**
- only revisit a covered topic if the next question is clearly deeper

So for `React`, if topics are:

- hooks
- state management
- forms
- rendering
- performance

and runtime knows `hooks` and `forms` were already asked, it can steer the model toward:

- rendering
- performance
- state management

instead of repeating hooks again.

## What I recommend implementing

For `skills_only` only:

- add `asked_question_signatures_by_skill` to runtime state
- populate it from assistant transcript lines
- inject `Already asked on this skill` into the compact memory message
- add a strict prompt line:
  - `Do not repeat the same question or same topic angle on the current skill unless the follow-up is clearly deeper and references the candidate's last answer.`
- if `topics` exist, prefer uncovered topics before repeating covered ones

## Short answer

How to avoid repeated questions in `skills_only` mode:

- do not rely on prompt wording alone
- add deterministic per-skill memory of already asked question angles
- inject that memory into the model context each turn
- prefer uncovered topics first
- only allow repetition when the next question is explicitly deeper

If you want, I can implement this next in the codebase.

## Assistant

Implemented the minimal reconnect-resume plan.

The agent-side reconnect flow in `agent-python/app/runner.py` now does three things better:

- disconnect tracking is symmetric, so `CandidateRoomTracker._on_disconnected(...)` only reacts to the expected candidate identity
- when the candidate reconnects within the grace window, the interviewer gives a short resume message instead of silently continuing
- that resume behavior works both during the main interview and during wrap-up

On the candidate side in `dashboard-react/src/pages/InterviewJoin.jsx`, the main live interview screen now shows a reconnect banner, not just the wrap-up phase. It tells the candidate the interview is not closed, reconnect is automatic, and it will continue from the same place once the network is stable. I also softened `handleRoomError(...)` so clearly recoverable mid-session connection glitches do not immediately throw the candidate into the full error screen after the room had already connected once.

I added focused Python tests for the reconnect-sensitive pieces:

- expected-candidate-only disconnect handling
- different resume instructions for live interview vs wrap-up

Verification passed:

- `python -m py_compile app/runner.py tests/test_interview_completion.py`
- `python -m unittest discover -s tests -p "test_interview_completion.py"`
- `npm run build` in `dashboard-react`

One important scope note remains: this still resumes from the same place only while the same running agent worker stays alive. It does not add database-based cross-process restoration, which we intentionally kept out for minimal change.

## Assistant

Updated `RECONNECT_GRACE_SECONDS` to `300` seconds in `agent-python/app/runner.py`.

That means the main interview will now wait up to 5 minutes for the candidate to reconnect before ending due to disconnect timeout. The existing resume behavior stays the same:

- if the candidate reconnects within that window, the interview continues from the same in-memory state
- the post-reconnect resume message still plays
- the candidate UI banner still shows reconnect status

One important detail: during final wrap-up, the reconnect wait is still capped by the remaining wrap-up time, because that path uses `min(RECONNECT_GRACE_SECONDS, remaining_wrap_up)`. So the 5-minute grace mainly helps during the main interview, not after wrap-up has already started.

Verification passed:

- `python -m py_compile app/runner.py`
- `python -m unittest discover -s tests -p "test_interview_completion.py"` with `37` tests passing

## Assistant

Here is what was implemented.

### Backend ([`backend-node/src/interviews/precheck-helpers.js`](c:\AIVoiceAgents\ai-calling-platform\backend-node\src\interviews\precheck-helpers.js), [`routes.js`](c:\AIVoiceAgents\ai-calling-platform\backend-node\src\interviews\routes.js), [`storage/proctor-frames.js`](c:\AIVoiceAgents\ai-calling-platform\backend-node\src\storage\proctor-frames.js))

- **`POST /api/interviews/session/precheck/meta`** – `{ joinToken }` → `sessionId`, `participantName`, `interviewTitle`, `instructions`, `rulesSummary` (JSON trimmed to 2000 chars), `linkExpiresAt`. Same session checks as resolve; **no** dispatch, LiveKit token, or recording.
- **`POST /api/interviews/session/precheck/audio`** – multipart `audio` + `joinToken`; WebM/WAV/OGG magic, min size, byte-variance heuristic; responds `{ ok, checks }`; best-effort `interview_events` row `precheck_audio_ok`. Audio is **not** stored.
- **`POST /api/interviews/session/precheck/identity`** – multipart `image` + `joinToken`; uploads via existing Azure helper to `…/precheck/…jpg`, inserts into **`interview_proctor_frames`** with `client_meta.precheck: true`.

### API client ([`dashboard-react/src/services/api.js`](c:\AIVoiceAgents\ai-calling-platform\dashboard-react\src\services\api.js))

- `getInterviewPrecheckMeta`, `uploadInterviewPrecheckAudio`, `uploadInterviewPrecheckIdentity`.

### React ([`InterviewPrecheck.jsx`](c:\AIVoiceAgents\ai-calling-platform\dashboard-react\src\pages\InterviewPrecheck.jsx), [`InterviewJoin.jsx`](c:\AIVoiceAgents\ai-calling-platform\dashboard-react\src\pages\InterviewJoin.jsx))

- New **`precheck`** phase on the same `/interview/join?token=…` URL: meta load → instructions → allow camera/mic → preview + level meter → identity snapshot upload → phrase + **record / stop & verify** (min ~2.5s) → checkbox → **Start interview**.
- **`resolveInterviewSession`** runs only when `phase === "resolve_loading"`, driven by a `useEffect` (not on first paint during precheck).
- **`sessionStorage`** key `interview_precheck_ok_v1_<token>` skips the gate on reload/retry in the same tab after a successful precheck.
- Main join footer branding is hidden during precheck so it isn’t duplicated with the precheck screen.

`npm run build` for `dashboard-react` completes successfully.

**Note:** Identity upload needs the same Azure storage config as proctor frames; if Azure is missing, uploads return 502, same as today’s proctor path.
